<div id="review_671877785" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/671877785" />
    <a title="Alejandro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro"><img alt="Alejandro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328672389p2/665584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/671877785?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alejandro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alejandro" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro">Alejandro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=detective">detective</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer671877785" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15462281968788613143">I like detective novels and I am a fan of J.K. Rowling, so when I found out that this "Robert Galbraith" was a pseudonym of Rowling, I thought that it was the perfect combination of elements that I have to read the book as soon as possible.<br/><br/>I have to admit that in good amount of the book I wasn't enjoying it so much. I was feeling it too slow, and nothing exciting was happening, since Cormoran Strike, the detective, wasn't doing much just asking questions to each witness and the events was gettin</span>
  <span id="freeText15462281968788613143" style="display:none">I like detective novels and I am a fan of J.K. Rowling, so when I found out that this "Robert Galbraith" was a pseudonym of Rowling, I thought that it was the perfect combination of elements that I have to read the book as soon as possible.<br /><br />I have to admit that in good amount of the book I wasn't enjoying it so much. I was feeling it too slow, and nothing exciting was happening, since Cormoran Strike, the detective, wasn't doing much just asking questions to each witness and the events was getting over and over, it was tedious.<br /><br />My anchor to keep reading it was Robin, the secretary of Strike, since she is a wonderful character that gives a way positive and radiant atmosphere to the book when she is in the scene. I think that besides that she is smart, proactive and good hearted, also she gets excited about being in the world of private detectives and that exciment was contagious with me.<br /><br />There are some detective teams that the lead character is so great that sometimes the "sidekick" doesn't get the proper credit, but here I have to tell you that Robin is as important to the effectiveness of the novel as Cormoran, the lead character.<br /><br />If you took her out of the formula, the magic (pun intended) would dissapear.<br /><br />Okay, as I was saying, the book was slow and there were too much details about the private life of Cormoran (I mean, why do I want to read about his nephew's birthday party or all the times that he goes to get a shower in the university campus?! Geez!) I want to read about the case and I really think that the book could have less length but I guess that when it's an author with the reputation of Rowling, they can't let to print a good book with a 300+ pages, no, it has to be 400+ or nothing. I wouldn't be surprised if the second book will get 500+ pages. But I really do hope that it would be with less pages.<br /><br />So, the book was slow, real slow, tedious interviews, but right when I was like 20% of finishing the book, bam! the tempo changed and all the pieces of the puzzle were starting to get into place, you get a good speed of narrative and then you see Cormoran Strike as an awesome detective worthy to be side-by-side with Philip Marlowe and Sam Spade.<br /><br />Also, I like that the character is smoking cigarrettes. I am not pro or against smoking, I just think that it's silly that nowadays almost all authors are like too much afraid of using characters with the habit of smoke like if that would alienate the readers. I am not here to discuss about medicine and health, I just say that a private detective looks cool smoking.<br /><br />So, <b>
  <u>if you decide to read this book, please finish it</u>
</b>, don't leave it in the middle of the reading because you're getting bored, I can guarantee you that the smashing ending with be worthy of keeping with the book until the great end.<br /><br />Bravo Rowling, you did it again! ;) <br /><br />If there is a second book in this series, I'll be there to read it too.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Update: (June-24-2014)</u>
</b><br /><br />Indeed there are now a second novel and I am man of my word ;) I am reading the second book now!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15462281968788613143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

A private eye with a silly name solves a murder mystery, and there is a long exposition at the end of the how and why. The characters are quite well drawn, and the writing is competent, but I wouldn't seek out any further books with the same star.<br/><br/>I didn't know, when I reviewed this, that it was written by J K Rowling! But it doesn't change my view.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Philip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Philip" href="/user/show/30863291-philip">Philip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=author-woman">author-woman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1642193933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16956472563662748905">3.5ish stars.<br/><br/>Far from perfect, but far from awful. Despite its many faults it's never less than highly readable and fluid. It's never particularly pulse-pounding but it somehow always held my attention.<br/><br/>It honestly isn't twisty or suspenseful enough for me. It's super streamlined and reads more or less like a series of neat, orderly interviews with each of the various players in the mystery. Even at the 11 o'clock reveal, there's never a sense of danger or serious tension, it's just the natural p</span>
  <span id="freeText16956472563662748905" style="display:none">3.5ish stars.<br /><br />Far from perfect, but far from awful. Despite its many faults it's never less than highly readable and fluid. It's never particularly pulse-pounding but it somehow always held my attention.<br /><br />It honestly isn't twisty or suspenseful enough for me. It's super streamlined and reads more or less like a series of neat, orderly interviews with each of the various players in the mystery. Even at the 11 o'clock reveal, there's never a sense of danger or serious tension, it's just the natural progression of things. Detective investigates mystery; detective follows lead 1; detective follows lead 2; repeat several more times; detective solves mystery; case closed. <br /><br />Cormoran's a decent character but I <i>really</i> could have done without being told 849 times how hairy he is. It seems like Rowling goes through each of his individual body parts to describe how hairy they all are. Maybe someone can explain to me why he has hot psychos and supermodels all wanting to bed him... Robin has plenty of page time but she really should have been featured a lot more! She's one of the best things the novel has going for it. <br /><br />I'm down to read book 2 but not in a rush.<br /><br /><a href="https://mrphilipslibrary.wordpress.com/2017/06/13/the-cuckoos-calling-cormoran-strike-1-by-robert-galbraith/" rel="nofollow noopener">Posted in Mr. Philip's Library</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16956472563662748905" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2077340765" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer698924585407999556">Oh, wow. <br/><br/>I’m speechless. I am speechless at how bad this was. <br/><br/>The only thing that kept me from quitting altogether was the characters. The only two, to be precise. <br/><br/>I was more interested in Strike and Robin’s personal lives than that sorry excuse for a mystery plot. <br/>The entire mystery/thriller (?) element of the book and the investigation process were so painfully and mind numbingly boring that not only did I forget every single character the moment they were no longer in the scene, I also seriou</span>
  <span id="freeText698924585407999556" style="display:none">Oh, wow. <br /><br />I’m speechless. I am speechless at how bad this was. <br /><br />The only thing that kept me from quitting altogether was the characters. The only two, to be precise. <br /><br />I was more interested in Strike and Robin’s personal lives than that sorry excuse for a mystery plot. <br />The entire mystery/thriller (?) element of the book and the investigation process were so painfully and mind numbingly boring that not only did I forget every single character the moment they were no longer in the scene, I also seriously couldn’t care less as to who murdered the model. I just couldn’t muster the mental fibre to give a shit. <br /><br />Strike and Robin were the only saving grace of this book. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="698924585407999556" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1942497532" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1942497532" />
    <a title="Melindam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36434323-melindam"><img alt="Melindam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484595601p2/36434323.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1942497532?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melindam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melindam" href="/user/show/36434323-melindam">Melindam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408704004" href="/book/show/17684327-the-cuckoo-s-calling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36434323-melindam?shelf=crime-detective-fiction">crime-detective-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1942497532" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15481700799873014558">I admit that I am not a great fan of contemporary detective fiction. I find most books are too grim, even perverted with gratuitous violence, or unnecessarily long-winded with too much forced, fake-philosophical contemplation from detectives instead of actual action.<br/><br/>So I am happy to say that I enjoyed JKR's debut detective novel a lot. The minus 1 star is for the writing, which had a superfluity of totally awkward metaphors & "artistic" descriptions & over-complicated sentences. This grated a bi</span>
  <span id="freeText15481700799873014558" style="display:none">I admit that I am not a great fan of contemporary detective fiction. I find most books are too grim, even perverted with gratuitous violence, or unnecessarily long-winded with too much forced, fake-philosophical contemplation from detectives instead of actual action.<br /><br />So I am happy to say that I enjoyed JKR's debut detective novel a lot. The minus 1 star is for the writing, which had a superfluity of totally awkward metaphors &amp; "artistic" descriptions &amp; over-complicated sentences. This grated a bit at the beginning, but as the story slowly, but surely drew me in, I forgot about them. <br /><br />The private detective, Cormoran Strike, was created along the much too-obvious cliche-panels of the contemporary mystery genre: ex-soldier with a past &amp; the scars of war (a missing leg), neglected child of an uncaring mother (the rock-star father is a bit of an unexpected, but good touch), at the brink of a dysfunctional relationship, who smokes &amp; drinks. Yet, to my surprise, I found him really likeable. His assistant, Robin was a refreshing ray of sunlight that is normally not allowed to dwell in this type of fiction, so well done, JKR.<br /><br />The investigation of the crime is classically &amp; nicely built-up: you get the pieces of the jigsaw puzzle to put the whole picture together. You are gradually introduced to the circle of potential perpetrators and presented with possible motives for the murder as you learn about the personality and background of the victim. JKR places her clues inconspicuously along with the red herrings, but you can pick them up &amp; discover the real motive fairly early in the narrative, if not the person of the murderer. Yet, the story remains interesting till the very end.<br /><br />I will most definitely read the next book of the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15481700799873014558" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_772046634" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/772046634" />
    <a title="Alex is The Romance Fox" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6663962-alex-is-the-romance-fox"><img alt="Alex is The Romance Fox" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1428866380p2/6663962.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/772046634?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex is The Romance Fox" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex is The Romance Fox" href="/user/show/6663962-alex-is-the-romance-fox">Alex is The Romance Fox</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/16160834-the-cuckoo-s-calling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6663962-alex-is-the-romance-fox?shelf=authors-a-h">authors-a-h</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6663962-alex-is-the-romance-fox?shelf=lendable">lendable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6663962-alex-is-the-romance-fox?shelf=adventure-mystery-crime-thriller">adventure-mystery-crime-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer772046634" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14847624335811675994">I’m about to reveal my secret!!!!!!!! I have purchased lots and lots of Harry Potter’s books – you know the time that every small and big kid wanted one….well, I gave them out as birthday and Christmas presents….but me…. I haven’t read any of them….though my son devoured each book and I have the entire series in my bookcase…I just haven’t had that “read me, read me” pull….Yes, truly!!!. <br/>I started book #1 and gave up after a couple of chapters. I know….I should have persevered but I did not…….may</span>
  <span id="freeText14847624335811675994" style="display:none">I’m about to reveal my secret!!!!!!!! I have purchased lots and lots of Harry Potter’s books – you know the time that every small and big kid wanted one….well, I gave them out as birthday and Christmas presents….but me…. I haven’t read any of them….though my son devoured each book and I have the entire series in my bookcase…I just haven’t had that “read me, read me” pull….Yes, truly!!!. <br>I started book #1 and gave up after a couple of chapters. I know….I should have persevered but I did not…….maybe one day…it did take me over 30 years to read the Lord of the Rings books (which I totally loved)...so who knows!! But wait, I am not doing a review on Harry Potter or Frodo! I’m writing about a totally different book altogether and the only connection to Magical Harry P is the author. <br><br>That’s right!!! A more different genre could have never been guessed by us veracious readers!!!– And if you haven’t read all the hype about her writing something not in same genre of Harry P and using a pseudonym…then you must be one of the very few people on this planet!! And if anyone ever believed that it was “overs” for JK after the epic and magical saga of Harry P..let me just say how wrong they would be!!! Yes, even despite all the hype and build-up.<br><br>A Cuckoo’s Calling by Robert Galbraith a.k.a J.K. Rolling is actually pretty good. No magic wands, no potions, witches and spells…here we have a good, gripping, and interesting mystery tale filled with supermodels, fame, family, murder, betrayal, greed that introduces a character that is not your hero norm, but wow…..by the end of the book….he’s become one of those unforgettable fiction characters that stay with you for a long time.<br><br>I loved the take on rockstars!!!!!!!!!!! <blockquote>
  <b> “Like other inveterate womanizers Strike had encountered, Duffield’s voice and mannerisms were slightly camp. Perhaps such men became feminized by prolonged immersion in women’s company, or perhaps it was a way of disarming their quarry.” </b>
</blockquote>Cormoran Strike is a private investigator whose business is not doing too well. One-legged (lost the other in Afghanistan fighting for Britain!!), overweight, bad dresser, not handsome in the least, homeless and living in his office – a total underdog!! Really!! his father, the ageing rock star who never married Cormoran’s dead groupie mother, is even demand interest on a loan he made to C!!! But under all that is an honorable and honest human being and that’s what pulls you in and has you wanting him to win all the obstacles in his life. <blockquote>
  <b> “Strike was used to playing archaeologist among the ruins of people’s traumatized memories;” </b>
</blockquote>Besides C, there are so many other memorable characters. Robin, his secretary was the other favorite of mine in this story <blockquote>
  <b>“Robin was disposed to feel desperately sorry for anyone with a less fortunate love life than her own – if desperate pity could describe the exquisite pleasure she actually felt at the thought of her own comparative paradise.” </b>
</blockquote>, about a murder of Lula Landry, a supermodel.<br><br>The writing style is really great - elegant prose that flows beautifully, keeping you turning page after page. <br><br>I loved the Englishness in this story……..I really smiled reading this……… <blockquote>
  <b> She looked away from him, drawing hard on her Rothman’s; when her mouth puckered into hard little lines around the cigarette, it looked like a cat’s anus. </b>
</blockquote> The imagery……<blockquote>
  <b>“Yeah,” he said.<br>Duffield had returned, holding another drink, cleaving his way back through the crowd, whose faces revolved after him, tugged by his aura. His legs in their tight jeans were like black pipe cleaners, and with his darkly smudged eyes he looked like a Pierrot gone bad. </b>
</blockquote>The settings in a dark<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385229411i/7103951.jpg" alt=" photo images3_zps12d97549.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> and gothic London <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385229411i/7103952.jpg" alt=" photo images1_zps52b4464e.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a href="http://s887.photobucket.com/user/ameliaandrade100/media/images2_zps84f1de1d.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385229411i/7103953.jpg" alt=" photo images2_zps84f1de1d.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> are so vividly written that you can feel the cold,<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385229411i/7103954.jpg" alt=" photo images_zpsa727ef55.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> the grayness <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385229411i/7103955.jpg" alt=" photo download_zps697004c4.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">and menace that surrounds this world of rock stars, supermodels, designers and the paparazzi.<a href="http://s887.photobucket.com/user/ameliaandrade100/media/download1_zps167fcf64.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385229411i/7103956.jpg" alt=" photo download1_zps167fcf64.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>Incredible sense of place and characters that brings it and them all to life.<br>Allright….let me just say – get this book, not because it’s a J.K. Rowling only but that it’s a great mystery read.<br>Some quotes that I thought were great…..<br><br><blockquote><b> “How easy it was to capitalize on a person’s own bent for self-destruction; how simple to nudge them into non-being, then to stand back and shrug and agree that it had been the inevitable result of a chaotic, catastrophic life.” <br><br>“The dead could only speak through the mouths of those left behind, and through the signs they left scattered behind them.” </b></blockquote> How true is this???? <blockquote><b>“Couples tended to be of roughly equivalent personal attractiveness, though of course factors such as money often seemed to secure a partner of significantly better looks than oneself.” </b></blockquote>And yes, I am hoping we get a bit more of Cormoran Strike. I loved his way of solving the case and it would make a great series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14847624335811675994" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_669146619" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/669146619" />
    <a title="Tomoe Hotaru" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5548051-tomoe-hotaru"><img alt="Tomoe Hotaru" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571221863p2/5548051.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/669146619?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tomoe Hotaru" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tomoe Hotaru" href="/user/show/5548051-tomoe-hotaru">Tomoe Hotaru</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=twas-good">twas-good</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer669146619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10918452310123317456"><b>
  <u>16 Jul' 2013</u>
</b> <br/><br/><b>
  <u>Full confession:</u>
</b> <br/>Pfft yeah, I totally did grab this after I heard it was written by <b>JK Rowling</b>? <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380227351i/681255.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Mostly because I hadn't even heard of this book prior to the news. But the blurb itself makes it sound like my type of novel on a cold, rainy day, regardless of the author.<br/><br/>Look, I'd like to pretend as if I were one of those people who wouldn't give a limp banana that <b>Rowling</b> wrote this book. I'd <i>love</i> to have the same level of self-restraint to cringe my nose in disgust and walk aw</span>
  <span id="freeText10918452310123317456" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>16 Jul' 2013</u>
</b> <br><br><b>
  <u>Full confession:</u>
</b> <br>Pfft yeah, I totally did grab this after I heard it was written by <b>JK Rowling</b>? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380227351i/681255.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Mostly because I hadn't even heard of this book prior to the news. But the blurb itself makes it sound like my type of novel on a cold, rainy day, regardless of the author.<br><br>Look, I'd like to pretend as if I were one of those people who wouldn't give a limp banana that <b>Rowling</b> wrote this book. I'd <i>love</i> to have the same level of self-restraint to cringe my nose in disgust and walk away from the bandwagon. <br>But, so help me God, I do love <b>Rowling</b>'s every bit of written word, and I cannot keep away from her dry British humour, her morbidly fascinating characters, and the thoroughness she puts into her work.<br><br>So, prigs to the left, please.<br><br><br>***<br><br><br><blockquote>
<i>Why did you die when the lambs were cropping?<br>You should have died at the apple's dropping,<br>when the grasshopper comes to trouble,<br>and the wheat-fields are sodden stubble,<br>And all the winds go sighing,<br>for sweet things dying.</i><br><br>-Christina G. Rossetti, "A Dirge"</blockquote><br>I knew <b>Rowling</b> was writing a crime novel for adults, which is why I was a little more than baffled when I picked up <i>The Casual Vacancy</i> and found it far from the murder-mystery I had been anticipating.<br>This -- <i>The Cuckoo's Calling</i> -- is that murder-mystery I have long been salivating over. And the long wait definitely paid off; I was not disappointed. <br>It starts on a grim, curious note. A young celebrity has died, plummeting to her untimely doom. And as <b>Rowling</b> does best, a note of glorified tension permeated this opening, drawing us from the very first turn of the page, into Lula Landry's tragic fate.<br>What follows is the investigation into her death, formally written off as mental-health-induced suicide, by the most unlikely of all heroes: Cormoran Strike and his assistant, Robin.<br><br>If you imagine a dashing, more contemporary version of Sherlock Holmes -- perhaps one Benedict Cumberbatch in all his dreamy-eyed glory -- you better put your panties back on because Strike is no poster-boy:<br><blockquote>
  <i>Her accidental assailant was massive; his height, his general hairiness, coupled with a gently expanding belly, suggested a grizzly bear.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>But no less do we come to admire this former military man. He is quick, he is astute, and he is very much human. Like always, the best part of <b>Rowling</b>'s work is her <b>
  <u>ability to craft such life-like characters</u>
</b>, whose problems and thoughts echo only too real, that no matter how bizarre or spectacular the events, we never for a second lose our immersion in the authenticity of her world.<br>The amount of care put into every description really does show in her prose. The small, contextual humour she manages to sneak into the narrative makes it feel as if we were sharing a secret.<br><br>This novel managed to be <b>
  <u>stimulating, engaging, and touching</u>
</b> at the same time. As leisurely as the plot unfolds, never did I lose interest in Strike's investigation. My favourite fact being that there actually <i>was</i> an investigation! (cue the gasps)<br>We are taken along for the ride; no clues or tidbits are left out from us readers, bereaving us from the chance of making our own accusations. No, we are kept invested in the outcome of Strike's investigation as if we were part of it ourselves. My suspicions shifted from one character to another, never making <i>The Cuckoo's Calling</i> a predictable nor boring read.<br><br>Strike and Robin's relationship -- initially tip-toeing on propriety -- admittedly worried me at first. This is where <i>you know</i> you've read one too many Young-Adult or self-proclaimed "Adult" novels, and actually expect <b>Rowling</b> to do the unforgivable and use the opportunity to build up romantic tension and, God forbid, the dreaded Love Triangle.<br>But this is <b>Rowling</b> we are talking about, and she steered way clear off <i>that</i> iceberg. Our two protagonists' chemistry remained friendly, albeit a little professional, before turning into the warm relationship a tutor might have with his apprentice. Of course if future books take this into another direction, we will see how I take it. In the meantime, I am keeping my fingers crossed.<br><br>It is dynamics such as these -- between characters, within characters -- that makes <i>The Cuckoo's Calling</i> such a multi-faceted and descriptive novel. We see characters through many others' eyes, and yet <b>
  <u>we are left to make our own judgements, never having our thoughts made up for us</u>
</b> like so many writers attempt to do.<br>The peak of the novel, although not exactly a <i>new</i> or never-before-seen turn of events, still came out as a surprise for me. The small details collided into a seamless blanket that covered everything nice and smoothly. I was very satisfied with the ending; no questions left unanswered, no forced bit of cliffhanger to goad us into buying the next book ...<br><br>So yes, I jumped on this bandwagon. And I do not regret it one bit.<br><br><br>***<br>&gt; My review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1027427051" rel="nofollow noopener">The Silkworm</a><br>&gt; My review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1583892784" rel="nofollow noopener">Career of Evil</a><br>&gt; You can also find more reviews at <a href="http://elfswood.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10918452310123317456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1339318058" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1339318058?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1339318058" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13574931730603778048"><b>Sale Alert: Kindle Deal Nov 1, 2020 <a href='https://www.amazon.com/dp/B00AA20E5Y/ref=s9_acsd_al_bw_c2_x_1_i?pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&pf_rd_s=merchandised-search-3&pf_rd_r=X55V3JR68VBV7E4P1VN1&pf_rd_t=101&pf_rd_p=c8976d75-8d62-4a60-ac0c-b18c52c214d6&pf_rd_i=7533915011' rel='nofollow noopener'>$2.99</a></b><br/><br/>After reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13497818.The_Casual_Vacancy' title='The Casual Vacancy by J.K. Rowling' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Casual Vacancy</a> I had decided that I probably wouldn’t read any of her adult fiction books. I didn’t expect it to be like Harry Potter but I really wasn’t expecting it to be more of a character study and it was really bleak. I was depressed after reading it. <b>I mention this because</b> I didn’t have very high hopes going into The Cuckoo’s Calling and therefore I am pleasantly surprised.<br/><br/>This is a pretty straight up who-dun-it. There isn’t a lot</span>
  <span id="freeText13574931730603778048" style="display:none"><b>Sale Alert: Kindle Deal Nov 1, 2020 <a href="https://www.amazon.com/dp/B00AA20E5Y/ref=s9_acsd_al_bw_c2_x_1_i?pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&amp;pf_rd_s=merchandised-search-3&amp;pf_rd_r=X55V3JR68VBV7E4P1VN1&amp;pf_rd_t=101&amp;pf_rd_p=c8976d75-8d62-4a60-ac0c-b18c52c214d6&amp;pf_rd_i=7533915011" rel="nofollow noopener">$2.99</a></b><br /><br />After reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13497818.The_Casual_Vacancy" title="The Casual Vacancy by J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">The Casual Vacancy</a> I had decided that I probably wouldn’t read any of her adult fiction books. I didn’t expect it to be like Harry Potter but I really wasn’t expecting it to be more of a character study and it was really bleak. I was depressed after reading it. <b>I mention this because</b> I didn’t have very high hopes going into The Cuckoo’s Calling and therefore I am pleasantly surprised.<br /><br />This is a pretty straight up who-dun-it. There isn’t a lot of action or anything like that it is an intellectual, interview the people and come up with the big picture. Think Rockford Files, Simon and Simon, Nancy Drew, Angel (without the vampires). <b> I’ve read where some people figured it out and knew who the killer was and to them I say BRAVO…cuz I failed completely.</b> Yes, all the clues were there and I should have been able to put it all together but I looked left when I totally should have looked right and so I was surprised. But I totally like it when I’m fooled.<br /><br />Strike is a likeable enough fellow. He is a bit down on his luck both professionally and personally but that is not going to stop him from trying to get something done. I was rooting for Strike he is pretty likable as a down-and-out-just-trying-to-pick-up-the-pieces-character.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Other people his age had houses and washing machines, cars and television sets, furniture and gardens and mountain bikes and lawnmowers: he had four boxes of crap, and a set of matchless memories.”</i>
</blockquote><br />He has a very easy repore with people and a way of getting them to talk, controlling the situation without seeming like he is controlling the situation and he was a bit of a romantic in some ways even if his own romance was completely in the toilet.<br /><br />Robin his new temporary secretary has always dreamed of a job like this, even if her new employer doesn’t seem excited to have her there. But she is going to make the most of this experience while she is looking for a permanent position. This was a very good start to a working relationship and hmmm….<b>could it go in the direction of a romantic entanglement eventually</b>. Well Robin does have a fiancé now but things can change. Can’t they? I definitely see a budding relationship of some sort there, whether it turns into a strong friendship later or more I’ll be fine either way. <i>But I think that dress will cause some problems...tehee</i><br /><br />Overall it was a decent mystery and I enjoyed the interviews with the various characters. There is quite a bit about Strike, his past, his current stalker and I liked diving into all of that. It made him feel far more real to me. <b> I will definitely be continuing on with this pseudonym of J.K Rowling. </b><br /><br /><i>I’m adding this just because it was my favorite conversation of the book and I do love drunken declarations. Strike is a bit of a romantic isn’t he</i><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>“R’bin,” he said, giving up and gazing down at her. “R’bin, d’you know wadda kairos mo…” He hiccoughed. “Mo…moment is?”<br /><br />“A kairos moment?” she repeated, hoping against hope it was not something sexual, something that she would not be able to forget afterwards, especially as the kebab shop owner was listening in and smirking behind them. “No, I don’t. Shall we go back to the office?”<br /><br />“You don’t know whadditis?” he asked, peering at her.<br /><br />“No.”<br /><br />“ ’SGreek,” he told her. “Kairos. Kairos moment. An’ it means,” and from somewhere in his soused brain he dredged up words of surprising clarity, “the telling moment. The special moment. The supreme moment.”<br /><br />Oh please, thought Robin, please don’t tell me we’re having one.<br /><br />“An’ d’you know what ours was, R’bin, mine an’ Charlotte’s?” he said, staring into the middle distance, his unlit cigarette hanging from his hand. “It was when she walk’d into the ward—I was in hosp’tal f’long time an’ I hadn’ seen her f’two years—no warning—an’ I saw her in the door an’ ev’ryone turned an’ saw her too, an’ she walked down the ward an’ she never said a word an,” he paused to draw breath, and hiccoughed again, “an’ she kissed me aft’ two years, an’ we were back together. Nobody talkin’. Fuckin’ beautiful. Mos’ beaut’ful woman I’ve ’ver seen. Bes’ moment of the whole fuckin’—’fmy whole fuckin’ life, prob’bly. I’m sorry, R’bin,” he added, “f’r sayin’ ‘fuckin’.’ Sorry ’bout that.”<br /><br />Robin felt equally inclined to laughter and tears, though she did not know why she should feel so sad.”</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_666991004" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/666991004" />
    <a title="Jon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4277731-jon"><img alt="Jon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384212540p2/4277731.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/666991004?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jon" href="/user/show/4277731-jon">Jon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4277731-jon?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer666991004" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6993330153426978970"> <a href='http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com/2013/08/the-cuckoos-calling-by-robert-galbraith.html#more' rel='nofollow noopener'> Check out Scott Reads It! for reviews, giveaways, & more!</a> <br/><br/> When it was revealed that J.K. Rowling had written a novel under the pseudonym, Robert Galbraith; I knew I had to read it. Rowling filled my childhood with magic, intrigue, and beauty with her Harry Potter series so I was eager to read her sophomore adult novel. It angers me how Rowling was betrayed by a friend who had revealed that she was the genius behind The Cuckoo's Calling. Every cloud does have it's silver lining and now, millio</span>
  <span id="freeText6993330153426978970" style="display:none"> <a href="http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com/2013/08/the-cuckoos-calling-by-robert-galbraith.html#more" rel="nofollow noopener"> Check out Scott Reads It! for reviews, giveaways, &amp; more!</a> <br /><br /> When it was revealed that J.K. Rowling had written a novel under the pseudonym, Robert Galbraith; I knew I had to read it. Rowling filled my childhood with magic, intrigue, and beauty with her Harry Potter series so I was eager to read her sophomore adult novel. It angers me how Rowling was betrayed by a friend who had revealed that she was the genius behind The Cuckoo's Calling. Every cloud does have it's silver lining and now, millions of people will be introduced to a clever mystery noir. Another silver lining is that Rowling will be donating her royalties from The Cuckoo's Calling to charity for the next 3 years. I'm still angered how someone could have betrayed Rowling in such a cruel manner.<br /><br /> The Cuckoo's Calling is a much stronger novel than The Casual Vacancy and will definitely appeal to a wider audience than her adult debut. The Cuckoo's Calling is filled with all of Rowling's signature wit and charm that readers love. It's extremely evident from the writing style that Rowling still has the ability to create a tour de force, a novel that will definitely be looked on fondly 50 years in the future. This novel is a triumphant return for the Queen of Literature and it proves that J.K's domain and prowess doesn't just extend to children's literature. <br /><br /> This is an impressive piece of literature that is filled with immense intrigue and mystery. Albeit the beginning does have it's faults and is a tad slow-paced, this novel was extremely riveting. From start to finish, The Cuckoo's Calling does have it's share of dull moments, but they are overshadowed by the brilliance of Cormoran Strike. This is the mystery novel that I've been waiting for!<br /><br /> This novel has all of the star qualities of Stieg Larsson's novel and BBC's Sherlock. Cormoran actually really reminded me of Dr. Watson from BBC's Sherlock (Martin Freeman). Maybe it's because of their military past or that they both are a bit troubled? I really liked Cormoran, but I thought that he should confront his girlfriend and move on. I wasn't a huge fan of Robin, Cormoran's secretary because I never learned too much about her. I really didn't like how Robin put up with her boyfriend, Matthew (I think) who kept on bossing her around and Robin didn't really act like anything was wrong with that. The whole plotline with Robin was extremely predictable right from when she was interested and was too simplistic.<br /><br /> The mystery in The Cuckoo's Calling is well-throughout with just enough intrigue to keep me peeled to the page. I actually had no idea who the killer was throughout the novel; I had my incorrect suspicions though. I really liked how Rowling explored the world of the media and celebrities in such an unique and unusual way. You never really see celebrities as actual people in novels, they are usually portrayed as these untouchable gods that ordinary people have to gloat over. The fact that Rowling to decide to add a layer of vulnerability to Landry, added an interesting touch to this book.<br /><br /> The Cuckoo's Calling is a novel worthy of immense praise. I'll admit that the only reason I read this book was because it was written by Rowling. I'm definitely eagerly awaiting the next installment in the Comoran Strike series and I can't wait to see what antics Strike and Robin get into next. Color me surprised, but I really enjoyed The Cuckoo's Calling! </span>
  <a data-text-id="6993330153426978970" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3566219332" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3566219332" />
    <a title="Amalia Gkavea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56789747-amalia-gkavea"><img alt="Amalia Gkavea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559158764p2/56789747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3566219332?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amalia Gkavea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amalia Gkavea" href="/user/show/56789747-amalia-gkavea">Amalia Gkavea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer609529906" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2843952073426907700">Two words for this: simply stunning.<br/><br/>Cormoran Strike is my new hero. What an absolutely fantastic character Robert Galbraith has created. I just love everything about him, his size, his lovely caring attitude and his fearless quest to uncover the truth of the apparent suicide of Lula Landry, supermodel. <br/><br/>Coromoran is hired by Lula's adoptive brother, John Bristow, to investigate her death as he doesn't believe she committed suicide, albeit the Police do and have ruled it so. There is also the very</span>
  <span id="freeText2843952073426907700" style="display:none">Two words for this: simply stunning.<br /><br />Cormoran Strike is my new hero. What an absolutely fantastic character Robert Galbraith has created. I just love everything about him, his size, his lovely caring attitude and his fearless quest to uncover the truth of the apparent suicide of Lula Landry, supermodel. <br /><br />Coromoran is hired by Lula's adoptive brother, John Bristow, to investigate her death as he doesn't believe she committed suicide, albeit the Police do and have ruled it so. There is also the very suspicious uncle of Lula and John, one Tony Landry, who is their mother's brother. John Bristow has hired Cormoran as he remembered him being friends with his younger brother. Charlie, who had sadly died at aged eight many years before. <br /><br />There then follows one of the best investigations I have had the pleasure of reading, and I honestly thought I had been watching a drama on TV as the characters are so vividly described, together with the whole process of Coromoran's extremely sharp brain. <br /><br />The writing is delicious and extremely descriptive and I literally couldn't put the book down until I had finished it, it was only my sleep deprived eyes that made me put it down each night! <br /><br />I think we have a new PI on the block now, so everyone had better watch out as he is good, very very good. Robin is his very very likeable and extremely efficient secretary and I love her commitment to Cormoran and his failing investigative business. <br /><br />I do have one complaint about this book and that is that it had to end. I am now left feeling extremely sad that I don't have Strike and Robin in my life and will have to wait until the sequel (hopefully) is out. Please please take note Mr Galbraith! <br /><br />Very high recommended. 20/10. </span>

<div id="review_1471994631" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1471994631" />
    <a title="K. Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17568354-k-elizabeth"><img alt="K. Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606078931p2/17568354.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1471994631?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K. Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K. Elizabeth" href="/user/show/17568354-k-elizabeth">K. Elizabeth</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=boring">boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=dnf-or-skimmed">dnf-or-skimmed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1471994631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13226657729487606714"><b>DNF</b><br/><br/>Ah, come on. Why couldn't I just enjoy a different series written by J.K. Rowling? I was really expecting to love this, which may be why I pretty much came to hate it. Or, at least I think so. What I'm trying to say is that my expectations were really high. I mean, <i>really</i> high. Still. I was so bored reading this that I opted to just sit and listen to music rather than read. And that literally never happens with me. I <i>always</i> read if I have time to.<br/><br/>All right, getting straight to the point: I di</span>
  <span id="freeText13226657729487606714" style="display:none"><b>DNF</b><br /><br />Ah, come on. Why couldn't I just enjoy a different series written by J.K. Rowling? I was really expecting to love this, which may be why I pretty much came to hate it. Or, at least I think so. What I'm trying to say is that my expectations were really high. I mean, <i>really</i> high. Still. I was so bored reading this that I opted to just sit and listen to music rather than read. And that literally never happens with me. I <i>always</i> read if I have time to.<br /><br />All right, getting straight to the point: I didn't like Robin and I didn't like Strike. Robin felt too bland and tiresome and Strike swore too much and reminded me of a drunk. So, like I said, I didn't like either of them which is why getting involved in their little lives of marriage and divorce meant little-to-nothing to me. It was all just white-noise and I found myself wanting to yawn.<br /><br />Another thing. Why were all of the side characters boring too? It was like this novel hit the snooze button (that was lame) because I struggled to keep my eyes open as I read - which is why I settled on listening to music. At least then I wouldn't be falling asleep as I tried to keep track of what every boring character was doing.<br /><br />What's also funny is how this novel wasn't "easy" to read - usually "easy" reads are the novels that bore me. But no. It was actually rather difficult. I was having a hard time keeping up with everything, with who was who, where things were. Ah, it just left me flustered and tired and disinterested. I didn't care for any of it.<br /><br />All in all, this is my first DNF of 2017 - so, that's quite a bummer. However, this novel is making me realize that maybe Crime Fiction novels aren't for me...since I never seem to enjoy them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13226657729487606714" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Reading Corner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46088881-reading-corner"><img alt="Reading Corner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440473163p2/46088881.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1456109911?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reading Corner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reading Corner" href="/user/show/46088881-reading-corner">Reading Corner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1456109911" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17132483945201097033">For me, this book didn't stand out especially in this genre. The plot wasn't very interesting and I only really found it exciting towards the last hundred pages. The best bit for me was the characters as I loved how well they were developed and how they interacted with others, especially Cormoran Strike.<br/> <br/>The story follows Cormoran Strike, a private investigator and ex military man who has been left with a severe injury as a reminder and has to cope mentally and physically with his injury. John B</span>
  <span id="freeText17132483945201097033" style="display:none">For me, this book didn't stand out especially in this genre. The plot wasn't very interesting and I only really found it exciting towards the last hundred pages. The best bit for me was the characters as I loved how well they were developed and how they interacted with others, especially Cormoran Strike.<br /> <br />The story follows Cormoran Strike, a private investigator and ex military man who has been left with a severe injury as a reminder and has to cope mentally and physically with his injury. John Bristow approaches him with a case linked to fame and tragedy as John requires Cormoran to investigate his sister, Lula Landry's apparent suicide. The famous supermodel allegedly jumped off her balcony but John believes it was murder.<br /> <br />The opening had me immediately hooked but this went downhill quickly with lack of action and tension. About a hundred pages could have been cut from this book as nothing of real significance happened and the story was long winded at times. The actual case wasn't very intriguing and I never felt a threat of danger or tension. At times, I found myself immensely bored and I just wanted to put down the novel. <br /> <br />However, I definitely did enjoy the characters specifically Cormoran, Robin and Guy Somé's small appearance. Cormoran is a complex, engrossing character who made a great protagonist and Robin, his temporary secretary was a fantastic addition as she is wonderfully curious, assertive and clever. Guy Somé is full of hilarious lines and his scene is without a doubt one of the best bits in the book and the funniest. <br /> <br />Towards the end, the novel became exciting and thrilling as the story finally began to unfold and things began to link together. The ending is nicely done with a slightly shocking twist but the way the clues weave in together with the solved mystery is brilliantly done.<br /> <br />J.K Rowling displayed versatility in writing different genres but to be honest, I think this book was mediocre and I'm not bothered about reading the next book unless I can find it cheap.</span>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_777215944" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/777215944" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4086118-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567611029p2/4086118.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/777215944?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/4086118-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=london">london</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=england">england</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer777215944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16689113799501440176">I root for this author to make a successful genre break from fantasy to mystery. The plot is clever and the characters wonderfully drawn, but the slow build-up and a bit of overreaching in the prose kept my overall pleasure level at about average. I am eager to see this novel grow as a series and have confidence it will do so. <br/><br/>It seems fitting that just as a favored literary mystery writer, Kate Atkinson, moves into fantasy, this favored fantasy writer makes an excursion toward literary mystery.</span>
  <span id="freeText16689113799501440176" style="display:none">I root for this author to make a successful genre break from fantasy to mystery. The plot is clever and the characters wonderfully drawn, but the slow build-up and a bit of overreaching in the prose kept my overall pleasure level at about average. I am eager to see this novel grow as a series and have confidence it will do so. <br /><br />It seems fitting that just as a favored literary mystery writer, Kate Atkinson, moves into fantasy, this favored fantasy writer makes an excursion toward literary mystery. I don’t hold that much stock in the appellation of “literary”, as purveyors of best-selling pot-boilers of one age can ascend toward “literature” status in another (e.g. Chandler). Regardless, it is fortunate that the things that matter most to me, these authors’ strengths in story-telling and character development, carry through on the transition in genre they both make. <br /><br />The story involves a young London private detective, Cormoran Strike, working a case of a model’s death by fall from a third-story balcony. The case is brought to him by a lawyer who is this Lula’s adoptive brother. The police judge the death of the celebrity a suicide due to her troubled background as a half-black child abandoned by her mother and a chaotic life with the wild crowd of the rich and famous. They discount the statement of a producer’s wife on the first floor, who heard an argument with a man preceding the plunge, as the fancy residence was too solidly built for such sound to carry. <br /><br />With the help of his brilliant new secretary from a temp agency, Robin, Strike delves for clues in the life of Lula’s wealthy adoptive family and that of her friends and lover in the fashion and entertainment world. We are treated to a tour of the club scene, the fashion business, and the movie crowd, all with journalists and paparazzi buzzing around. At the other side of things, the drug culture of her boyfriend and the homeless world of a special friend of Lula’s from rehab. A bit too many threads for me to keep a hungry mind focused on the mystery, especially when the diversions and red herrings span a few hundred pages. Agatha Christie could juggle a dozen clues, threads, and characters within a couple of hundred pages. The lingering with so many slices of life here would be fine the author intends a sociological analysis of a broad scope of contemporary London culture. I ended up only feeling slightly guilty over my welcoming reaction to a second body in the story. Ultimately, a clever ending left me zinging and nicely points the way for some follow-up tales with the duo. <br /><br />Like Atkinson’s Jackson Brodie, Galbraith’s Cormoran Strike is ex-military and has somewhat the heart of a Boy Scout. Though rarely called upon for dangerous protective or defensive action, we can take a bit of comfort in knowing that capacity is there when needed (if they don't stupidly walk into a crisis without remembering their weapons). Unlike most of the bruised souls solving crimes in popular fiction, both are emotionally healthy and not too bitter over losses and bad cards dealt them in the past. They are refreshingly free of addictions or do not wallow in cynicism. Tough but tender has been done before, but I’ll take it gladly for a hero. <br /><br />I was a bit wary at Galbraith giving Strike such a sentiment-stirring vulnerability as a prosthetic leg, the result of his tour in Afghanistan. Sort of like humbling our potential superman with Kryptonite. Maybe there is some homage here to comics. Robin is just so good-hearted. Then again, she goes well beyond Lois Lane in providing timely and effective help with his case. And there is some grit to his life, as his break-up with his girlfriend leaves him living in his office and short on the rent. The larger satisfaction for me with the book lies not with solving the case, but in the understated, underground romance between Strike and his Girl Friday. As fair warning, I was sappy enough to be bowled over by the romance in King’s “11/23/63.” <br /><br />The writing is usually appropriately invisible. Sometimes it shines. Like when the Strike is reading the people he interviews for the investigation. Here his perceptions of a pair of socialite sisters are written in a way that aids the reader’s visualization and convey tinges of his male working-class consciousness:<br /><i>They were both as pristine and polished as life-size dolls recently removed from their cellophane boxes; rich-girl thin, almost hipless in their tight jeans, with tanned faces that had a waxy sheen especially noticeable on their foreheads, their long, gleaming dark manes with center partings, spirit-level exactitude. Her eyes were fractionally too close together, and the Botox and fillers could not smooth away the petulance in her expression.</i><br /><br />But doesn’t this come close to calling attention to the fine writing, disrupting your immersion in the scene? I don’t think so in this case. But check out the following example of Strike’s perception of a fashion designer friend of Lula’s: <br /><i>His face contrasted strangely with his taut, lean body, for it abounded in exaggerated curves: the eyes exophthalmic so they appeared fishlike, looking out of the sides of his head. The cheeks were round, shining apples and full-lipped mouth was a wide oval; his small head was almost perfectly spherical. Some looked as though he had been carved out of soft ebony by a master hand that had grown bored with its own expertise, and started to veer towards the grotesque.</i><br /><br />To me this feels like jarring and awkward overwriting. All in all such bits didn’t disrupt my pleasure much. I just leave some room for improvement in rating stars on the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16689113799501440176" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('G0kEkO2E2OrbnMNpjDFtyBpFy6Ui/H4tyIlnsrb5bXmXwMa6hrFrs72L71qFejHMY0CvsrJE7FBtWCj/xlL8dg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aP6tCcEDgyx31HFaYpoVUflP6CcZA+LQxqcCCjxLKRbkd28jqjYwdRHDXWlr0UlVgEqMMIm7cK1jdk1HTOC4GQ==')})
  }
//]]>

He and Robin have finally managed to re-establish their usual <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText11119499977411984480\" style=\"display:none\">Having solved two high profile homicide investigations with the assistance of his sidekick Robin Ellacott, private investigator Cormoran Strike is recovering from his newfound popularity. He and Robin have finally managed to re-establish their usual work routine, when they receive an extremely unusual package: one that contains a severed leg from a female. The incident causes Strike to reflect on the many individuals he’s crossed in the path, and to wonder just how many might be looking for revenge. He makes a list of these men for the police detectives working the case, but it seems like the officers don’t take Strike’s concerns very seriously. Cormoran and Robin make the decision to pursue their own independent investigation.  Their search for information leads them to some of London’s shadier neighborhoods, as they seek information on the men on Strike’s list of suspects. Dead end after dead end frustrates them. Unfortunately, it appears the owner of the leg isn’t the killer’s only victim—more bodies appear and the association with Strike hurts his business. Cormoran and Robin need to solve this case before their agency goes belly up.  Please note that this is key takeaways and analysis of the book and NOT the original book. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer548455569535596760"><i>This is a pseudonym for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1077326.J_K_Rowling' rel='nofollow noopener'> J.K. Rowling</a>, the author of the Harry Potter series and </i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13497818-the-casual-vacancy' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Casual Vacancy,</a><i> a novel for adults.</i><br/><br/><i>
  <b>NOTE: There is more than one author with this name on Goodreads.</b>
</i><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7171901.Robert_Galbraith' rel='nofollow noopener'>Robert Galbraith - Marine Biologist</a><br/><br/>Rowling was born to Anne Rowling (née Volant) and Peter James Rowling, a Rolls-Royce aircraft engineer, on 31 July 1965 in Yate, Gloucestershire, England, 10 miles (16 km) north</span>
  <span id="freeText548455569535596760" style="display:none"><i>This is a pseudonym for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1077326.J_K_Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener"> J.K. Rowling</a>, the author of the Harry Potter series and </i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13497818-the-casual-vacancy" rel="nofollow noopener">The Casual Vacancy,</a><i> a novel for adults.</i><br /><br /><i>
  <b>NOTE: There is more than one author with this name on Goodreads.</b>
</i><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7171901.Robert_Galbraith" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Galbraith - Marine Biologist</a><br /><br />Rowling was born to Anne Rowling (née Volant) and Peter James Rowling, a Rolls-Royce aircraft engineer, on 31 July 1965 in Yate, Gloucestershire, England, 10 miles (16 km) northeast of Bristol. Her mother Anne was half-French and half-Scottish. Her parents first met on a train departing from King's Cross Station bound for Arbroath in 1964. They married on 14 March 1965. Her mother's maternal grandfather, Dugald Campbell, was born in Lamlash on the Isle of Arran. Her mother's paternal grandfather, Louis Volant, was awarded the Croix de Guerre for exceptional bravery in defending the village of Courcelles-le-Comte during the First World War.<br /><br />Rowling's sister Dianne was born at their home when Rowling was 23 months old. The family moved to the nearby village Winterbourne when Rowling was four. She attended St Michael's Primary School, a school founded by abolitionist William Wilberforce and education reformer Hannah More. Her headmaster at St Michael's, Alfred Dunn, has been suggested as the inspiration for the Harry Potter headmaster Albus Dumbledore.<br /><br />As a child, Rowling often wrote fantasy stories, which she would usually then read to her sister. She recalls that: "I can still remember me telling her a story in which she fell down a rabbit hole and was fed strawberries by the rabbit family inside it. Certainly the first story I ever wrote down (when I was five or six) was about a rabbit called Rabbit. He got the measles and was visited by his friends, including a giant bee called Miss Bee." At the age of nine, Rowling moved to Church Cottage in the Gloucestershire village of Tutshill, close to Chepstow, Wales. When she was a young teenager, her great aunt, who Rowling said "taught classics and approved of a thirst for knowledge, even of a questionable kind," gave her a very old copy of Jessica Mitford's autobiography, Hons and Rebels. Mitford became Rowling's heroine, and Rowling subsequently read all of her books.<br /><br />Rowling has said of her teenage years, in an interview with <i>The New Yorker,</i> "I wasn’t particularly happy. I think it’s a dreadful time of life." She had a difficult homelife; her mother was ill and she had a difficult relationship with her father (she is no longer on speaking terms with him). She attended secondary school at Wyedean School and College, where her mother had worked as a technician in the science department. Rowling said of her adolescence, "Hermione [a bookish, know-it-all Harry Potter character] is loosely based on me. She's a caricature of me when I was eleven, which I'm not particularly proud of." Steve Eddy, who taught Rowling English when she first arrived, remembers her as "not exceptional" but "one of a group of girls who were bright, and quite good at English." Sean Harris, her best friend in the Upper Sixth owned a turquoise Ford Anglia, which she says inspired the one in her books.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="548455569535596760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
